	/c/search_results.cfm?vnet=0&site%5Fid=9533&t731=203535&jb=8490290 :: 124 :: 	Dean, College of Engineering, Agriculture, and Technology :: 125 :: 	Job ID: :: 126 :: 	8490290 :: 127 :: 	Position Title: :: 128 :: 	Dean, College of Engineering, Agriculture, and Technology :: 129 :: 	Company Name: :: 130 :: 	Oklahoma State University :: 131 :: 	Location(s): :: 132 :: 	Stillwater, Oklahoma, 74078, United States :: 133 :: 	Posted: :: 134 :: 	August 17, 2011 :: 135 :: Job Function: :: 136 :: Education, Non-Consulting :: 137 :: Entry Level: :: 138 :: No :: 139 :: 	Save Job :: 140 :: 	# :: 141 :: 	E-mail Job :: 142 :: 	# :: 143 :: 	Print Job :: 144 :: 	# :: 145 :: 	Apply For Job :: 146 :: 	# :: 147 :: 	Job Description :: 148 :: 	The Board of Regents for Oklahoma State University invites nominations and applications for the position of Dean, College of Engineering, Architecture and Technology. The Dean reports to the Provost & Senior Vice President for Academic Affairs. :: 149 :: Oklahoma State University, with a 120-year history, is one of the nation's most comprehensive land-grant university systems. The University has more than 33,000 students, 7,400 staff members, and campuses located in Stillwater, Tulsa, Oklahoma City and Okmulgee. Exceptional strength in the sciences, engineering, and architecture is a distinguishing feature of the University. :: 150 :: The College of Engineering, Architecture and Technology includes the oldest and largest engineering program, the only TAC/ABET accredited engineering technology programs and the oldest architecture program in Oklahoma. The three major curricular areas relate in a synergistic way and provide an unusually broad range of instructional, research and outreach/public service programs. This combination of Engineering, Architecture, and Technology programs within a single college is unique in the nation. With an enrollment of almost 3000 undergraduate and 700 graduate students, the College offers bachelor's, master's and doctoral degrees in engineering; bachelor's degrees in architecture, architectural engineering, and in engineering technology. All undergraduate programs are accredited at the program level. Undergraduate and graduate level academic programs are offered on the main campus in Stillwater, at the OSU-Tulsa campus, and through distance education. :: 151 :: With the quality of the current faculty, and the world-class facilities in Stillwater and Tulsa, and 38 endowed chairs and professorships, the college is poised to embark on a new era of excellence in education and engagement in discovery and innovation with broad impact. Further information about the programs and uniqueness of the College of Engineering, Architecture and Technology can be found at :: 152 :: http://www.ceat.okstate.edu/ :: 153 :: http://www.ceat.okstate.edu/ :: 154 :: . :: 155 :: <EM> RESPONSIBILITIES: </EM> :: 156 :: The Dean of the College of Engineering, Architecture and Technology is responsible for advancing excellence and innovation in all facets of the College including disciplinary and interdisciplinary academic, research and outreach programs; planning in multiple dimensions; faculty recruitment; faculty and staff development and recognition; student recruitment, enrichment and recognition; diversity; accountability standards; financial management; new facilities and facilities renovation; resource development and allocation; stewardship; alliances with various constituents of the College; and marketing the distinctive signature of the College. The Dean is accessible to all stakeholders, collaborative, and a compelling advocate and spokesperson for the College. :: 157 :: <EM> QUALIFICATIONS: </EM> :: 158 :: Candidates should have demonstrated intellectual leadership that inspires others; innovative and strategic management skills; a strong belief in the role and mission of a land-grant university; a broad knowledge of higher education; an understanding of scholarship and the value of interdisciplinary collaboration; an understanding of the issues and opportunities in education and research impacting on the College; an ability to create opportunities and alliances that advance the College; a demonstrated capacity to work effectively with faculty, students, and leaders at OSU and other educational agencies and institutions; evidence of ability to promote research and scholarly activity; and evidence of ability to lead a capital campaign and attract and manage external funding. Required qualifications include an earned doctorate; a record of scholarly achievement in research and teaching that meets qualifications for tenure and rank of professor in a discipline in the college and membership on the Graduate Faculty; a minimum of three years of administrative experience in engineering, architecture or engineering technology education at a comprehensive research university, or the equivalent; and the ability to work and communicate effectively with all publics served by the College. :: 159 :: <EM> SALARY: </EM> :: 160 :: Commensurate with qualifications. :: 161 :: <EM> BEGINNING DATE: </EM> :: 162 :: As soon as possible following acceptance of position. :: 163 :: <EM> APPLICATION: </EM> :: 164 :: Inquiries about the search may be directed to the committee chair, Dr. Peter Sherwood, at peter.sherwood@okstate.edu. Applications will be accepted until the position is filled. :: 165 :: Nominations and application materials must be submitted electronically (MSWord strongly preferred) to: :: 166 :: <STRONG> OKStateCEATDean@academic-search.com </STRONG> :: 167 :: . Application materials will be accepted until the position is filled. Application materials should include a letter indicating the applicant's interest, experience and qualifications for the position, a curriculum vitae and the names, addresses, telephone numbers and email addresses of five professional references who will not be contacted without prior notification. :: 168 :: Assisting in the search is: :: 169 :: <STRONG> Robert W. Lawless, Ph.D., Senior Consultant </STRONG> :: 170 :: <STRONG> Academic Search, Inc. </STRONG> :: 171 :: rwl@academic-search.com :: 172 :: mailto:rwl@academic-search.com :: 173 :: <STRONG> 806.799.1329 or 918.284.1395 </STRONG> :: 174 :: A position profile may be found at :: 175 :: www.academic-search.com :: 176 :: http://www.academic-search.com/ :: 177 :: under Current Searches. Interested individuals are encouraged to visit :: 178 :: www.okstate.edu :: 179 :: http://www.okstate.edu/ :: 180 :: for additional information. :: 181 :: <EM> ~ </EM> :: 182 :: <EM> Oklahoma </EM> :: 183 :: <EM> State University </EM> :: 184 :: <EM> is an Affirmative Action/Equal Employment Opportunity E-Verify Employer committed to diversity. <STRONG> The University of Akron: </STRONG> :: 160 :: For more than 130 years, The University of Akron has been an active participant in Akron's renaissance of commercial and artistic endeavor, a leader in the metropolitan area's intellectual and professional advancement, a center for internationally lauded research efforts, and a source of enrichment, education, and vitality for Northeast Ohio. The University of Akron is 30 miles south of Cleveland and is a publicly assisted institution. UA is the public research university for Northern Ohio. The Princeton Review listed UA among the Best in the Midwest in its 2008 edition of Best Colleges: Region-by-Region. Serving nearly 29,000 students, the university offers approximately 300 associate, bachelor's, master's, doctoral and law degree programs and 100 certificate programs at sites in Summit, Wayne, Medina and Holmes counties. The campus is among the most modern in the region, with 9 new buildings, 14 major renovations, and 30 acres of new green space. For more information please visit the University of Akron's homepage at: www.uakron.edu :: 161 :: <STRONG> The University of Akron's School of Communication: </STRONG> :: 162 :: The School has 24 full-time faculty and approximately 1,100 undergraduate students and 40 graduate students. Enrollment has grown significantly over the past five years. The School offers B.A. degree programs in organizational communication, public relations, interpersonal and public communication, mass-media (radio/TV, media production), and news. The School also offers an M.A. degree. Please visit our website to learn more about our undergraduate and graduate program: www.uakron.edu/schlcomm :: 163 :: Job Requirements :: 164 :: An earned doctorate in Communication or related field by August 2012 required. In addition to other duties, the selected candidate will interact with and escort state inspectors, architects, and engineers on inspection visits. It is essential that the selected candidate be highly organized and an enthusiastic self-starter. This position necessitates excellent verbal/writing skills to include writing reports and entering work order data. The ability to read blue prints and interpret construction/record drawings is essential. The selected candidate may instruct, train, review, and evaluate the preventive maintenance work of technicians and trades people. This position requires extensive physical activities to include walking, climbing, and stooping; use of personal protective equipment; class/testing in infectious diseases; ladder climbing; and accessing tight spaces. In addition to proven experience in the above activities, preferred minimum training and experience include graduation from a four-year college with a major in Architecture, Electrical Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, Civil Engineering, or Construction Management and two years of progressive experience in the construction or renovation of buildings and building systems. Candidates should possess a valid NC driver's license and be eligible to operate a state-owned vehicle in accordance with the ECU property policy. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: <STRONG> Minimum Qualifications </STRONG> :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: Associate's degree in the assigned discipline; or equivalent combination of training and experience. Job :: 160 :: 	# :: 161 :: 	E-mail Job :: 162 :: 	# :: 163 :: 	Print Job :: 164 :: 	# :: 165 :: 	Apply For Job :: 166 :: 	# :: 167 :: 	Job Description :: 168 :: 	New Mexico Tech’s Dept. of Earth and Environmental Science ( :: 169 :: www.ees.nmt.edu :: 170 :: http://www.ees.nmt.edu/ :: 171 :: ) seeks applications for a post-doctoral fellow in mountain hydrology with an emphasis on the role of deep groundwater. The appointment, funded by NSF, will support a project investigating :: 172 :: hydrologic impacts of climate change on snow-dominated mountain watersheds in northern New Mexico and southern Colorado. The project integrates new physical, chemical and isotopic measurements as well as :: 173 :: existing spatial/temporal data sets, remote sensing imagery, and downscaled regional climate-modeling products with new 4D coupled surface-ground water models at the 1000 km :: 174 :: <SUP> 2 </SUP> :: 175 :: scale. Research goals include identifying flow paths and determining residence times, with an ultimate goal of quantifying hydrologic response in downstream irrigated mountain valleys. :: 176 :: Applicants should have a demonstrated ability to independently conduct field investigations, utilize large data sets, and develop hydrologic simulation studies. Ability to generate new research questions and develop an approach to their answers is desired. The appointment is for one year with an option for a second year. Working collaboratively with the project PI, students, and staff, the successful candidate will lead research activities within the project that generate the submission of two or more peer-reviewed publications each year. :: 177 :: <STRONG> Interested applicants should email a CV, transcripts, one relevant publication, a one-page statement of past and present research goals, and the names and addresses of three references to Professor John L. Wilson ( </STRONG> :: 178 :: jwilson@nmt.edu :: 179 :: mailto:jwilson@nmt.edu :: 180 :: <STRONG> ) by September 30, 2011. </STRONG> :: 181 :: Job Requirements :: 182 :: Working with students, staff and the PI, the Post-Doc is expected to see to the (1) successful installation, maintenance, and operation of field instrumentation, (2) the downloading, analysis and synthesis of data and incorporation into the New Mexico EPSCoR database, (3) the collection of water chemistry and water isotope samples to identify flow paths and residence times in study watersheds, (4) the successful development, calibration, testing, and operation of 4D numerical simulation models of two or more watersheds emphasizing the role of deep groundwater, (5) the successful interfacing of the watershed models with downscaled regional climate models in collaboration with climate scientists, (6) the successful deployment of the integrated model to examine watershed response to climate perturbations, and( 7) the successful submission of two or more manuscripts to peer-reviewed journals describing scientific findings in the NSF supported New Mexico EPSCoR hydrology project. :: 183 :: The position requires the completing of a PhD prior to appointment. Other important skills include programing (Fortran, C, C++, and/or Matlab), experience with HPC, training and experience with GIS, and :: 184 :: experience with meterological and hydrological field instrumentation. :: 185 :: APPLY FOR THIS JOB :: 186 :: Contact Person: :: 187 :: John L Wilson :: 188 :: Email Address: :: 189 :: jwilson@nmt.edu :: 190 :: mailto:jwilson@nmt.edu :: 191 :: Phone: :: 192 :: 575-835-5634 :: 193 :: Fax: :: 194 :: 575-835-6436 :: 195 :: Save Job :: 196 :: # :: 197 :: E-mail Job :: 198 :: # :: 199 :: Print Job :: 200 :: # :: 201 :: Apply For Job :: 202 :: # :: 203 :: 	Back to Results :: 204 :: 	/c/search_results.cfm?vnet=0&t735=&t730=&max=100&site%5Fid=9533&t731=&jb=8512218 :: 205 :: 	<BR/> :: 206 :: 	<B> Questions/Feedback </B> :: 207 :: 	<BR/> :: 208 :: 	If you need assistance or have feedback about this service :: 209 :: 	contact customer service :: 210 :: 	mailto:custserv@jobtarget.com :: 211 :: 	. :: 212 :: 	http://careers.insightintodiversity.com:80/images/spacerclear.gif :: 213 :: 	<BR/> :: 214 :: 	INSIGHT Into Diversity is the largest and oldest diversity employment magazine and website in higher education today. :: 215 :: 	<BR/> :: 216 :: 	Launched 35 years ago as a resource to assist institutions in complying with equal opportunity employment laws, :: 217 :: 	<BR/> :: 218 :: 	INSIGHT Into Diversity is now a premier source of information for half a million readers each month seeking in-depth news, :: 219 :: 	<BR/> :: 220 :: 	reports and commentary on issues surrounding all aspects of diversity and inclusion. Massachusetts Institute of Technology (MIT). The goal of the Institute is to develop, over a period of years, indigenous R&D capacity in Abu Dhabi, addressing issues of importance to the region in critical areas such as: renewable energy, sustainability, environment, water resources and microelectronics. The Institute offers graduate degree programs (MSc & PhD) in science and engineering disciplines with a focus on advanced energy and sustainable technologies (See :: 150 :: http://www.masdar.ac.ae/ :: 151 :: http://www.masdar.ac.ae/ :: 152 :: and :: 153 :: http://web.mit.edu/mit-tdp/index.html :: 154 :: http://web.mit.edu/mit-tdp/index.html :: 155 :: ). :: 156 :: <STRONG> CHEMICAL ENGINEERING (ChE) </STRONG> :: 157 :: The Chemical Engineering Program at Masdar Institute of Science and Technology invites applicants for positions at the Assistant, Associate and Full Professor levels. :: 158 :: <STRONG> Job Responsibilities: </STRONG> :: 159 :: The search is open to candidates with the following expertise: :: 160 :: Develop and teach graduate courses, supervise master's and doctoral students, develop a research program, seek external funding for such research, and participate in the Institute's service and outreach activities. :: 161 :: The successful applicant will have demonstrated research excellence in at least one of the following areas: :: 162 :: · applied thermodynamics :: 163 :: · process systems engineering :: 164 :: · chemical kinetics :: 165 :: · bioengineering :: 166 :: · separation processes :: 167 :: · transport processes :: 168 :: Job Requirements :: 169 :: Applicants should have: :: 170 :: (a) Ph.D. degree in Chemical Engineering or a closely related field, :: 171 :: (b) the ability to teach at the graduate level, :: 172 :: (c) the ability to supervise graduate students, :: 173 :: (d) an interest in research that addresses systems solutions to chemical process and/or renewable energy technology challenges. :: 174 :: <STRONG> Application submittal information: </STRONG> :: 175 :: Massachusetts Institute of Technology is assisting Masdar Institute in the search. </STRONG> :: 155 :: <BR/> :: 156 :: The Department of Cardiovascular Sciences at the East Carolina University Brody School of Medicine seeks a board eligible/certified Vascular Surgeon for a full-time faculty position with our Section of Vascular and Endovascular Surgery. The Section practices within the new East Carolina Heart Institute, touting world-class inpatient and outpatient facilities. The group maintains a high-volume open surgical practice encompassing all aspects of vascular reconstruction. In addition, there is a robust endovascular program, with full access to imaging equipment. There is a significant potential for clinical volume growth in a region with a high prevalence of vascular disease. The section is supported by full-time research personnel, and has productive clinical and basic science research projects underway. The applicant will be actively involved in the teaching and clinical training of medical students, surgical residents and Vascular Surgery fellows. In 2008, we opened a state-of-the-art 150 bed heart hospital, and a 225,000 square foot comprehensive cardiovascular outpatient facility with research space. Consequently, this is a unique opportunity for newly-recruited faculty to develop an outstanding academic career. The ECU Brody School of Medicine is affiliated with Pitt County Memorial Hospital. PCMH is the flagship hospital for University Health Systems of Eastern Carolina and serves as the teaching hospital for the Brody School of Medicine at East Carolina University. Fixed term or tenure track position available. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: <STRONG> Minimum Qualifications </STRONG> :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: The applicant must be certified or eligible for the Vascular Surgery Board of the American Board of Surgery and have completed an ACGME-accredited fellowship in Vascular Surgery. Applicants should have strong open and endovascular surgical skills, and a commitment to research and teaching within a university system. :: 162 :: <BR/> :: 163 :: <BR/> :: 164 :: <STRONG> Special Instructions to Applicants </STRONG> :: 165 :: <BR/> :: 166 :: East Carolina University requires applicants to submit a candidate profile online in order to be considered for the position. 173 :: The University of Arkansas at Little Rock (UALR) College of Business invites applications for a tenure-track position in Management (concentration in production/operations) (R97619). Starting August 15, 2012. :: 174 :: <BR/> :: 175 :: <BR/> :: 176 :: Responsibilities: Teach undergraduate/graduate courses in operations management and supply chain management, and related areas. Ability to teach classes in inventory management and/or project management preferred. Must demonstrate (1) the ability to provide instructional excellence in undergraduate/graduate courses in areas of specialization; (2) a planned research agenda consistent with expectations of an AACSB-accredited program; (3) interest in participating in student-centered service activities both at the college and university level; and (4) commitment to diversity and university initiatives supportive of diversity. Corporate/business work experience is desirable. :: 177 :: <BR/> :: 178 :: <BR/> :: 179 :: Qualifications: Ph.D. in business or D.B.A. with an emphasis in operations management (ABD acceptable). Must have terminal degree in hand or have completed all requirements for the terminal degree by appointment date. Official transcripts will be required prior to appointment. :: 180 :: <BR/> :: 181 :: <BR/> :: 182 :: The University of Arkansas at Little Rock is a Carnegie II research intensive institution with a metropolitan university mission. Founded in 1927 and part of the University of Arkansas system since 1969, UALR serves a diverse population of approximately 13,000 students. See the UALR website at :: 183 :: http://www.ualr.edu :: 184 :: http://www.ualr.edu :: 185 :: for more information about UALR. Little Rock is the capital of Arkansas, a metropolitan area with a population of 650,000 and more than a million people living within an hourâ€™s drive of downtown. It combines metropolitan convenience with a small-town feel and moderate cost of living. For more on Little Rock visit :: 186 :: http://www.littlerockchamber.com/about_little_rock.htm :: 187 :: http://www.littlerockchamber.com/about_little_rock.htm :: 188 :: . :: 189 :: <BR/> :: 190 :: <BR/> :: 191 :: The College of Business is AACSB accredited and is ranked among Best Business Programs by the US News and World Report, Best Colleges Edition, 2011. :: 192 :: <BR/> :: 193 :: <BR/> :: 194 :: To Apply: Send a letter of application addressing qualifications (Reference R97619), current vitae, student evaluations, teaching philosophy, and research interests/agenda, to Dr. Joe T. Felan; College of Business; University of Arkansas at Little Rock; 2801 South University, Little Rock, AR 72204; phone: 501.569.3383. Electronic submissions preferred: :: 195 :: jtfelan@ualr.edu :: 196 :: mailto:jtfelan@ualr.edu :: 197 :: . Review of applications will begin immediately and will continue until the job is filled. Benefits and salary are competitive. :: 198 :: <BR/> :: 199 :: <BR/> :: 200 :: This position may be subject to a pre-employment criminal background and sex offender registry check and drug screening. A criminal conviction or arrest pending adjudication shall not disqualify an applicant in the absence of a relationship to the requirements of the position. Background check and drug screening information will be used in a confidential, non-discriminatory manner consistent with state and federal law. :: 201 :: <BR/> :: 202 :: <BR/> :: 203 :: The University of Arkansas at Little Rock is an equal opportunity, affirmative action employer and actively seeks the candidacy of minorities, women, and persons with disabilities. patients with cancer disease. :: 	E-mail Job :: 156 :: 	# :: 157 :: 	Print Job :: 158 :: 	# :: 159 :: 	 	 	Job Description :: 160 :: 	<STRONG> Group, Network, or Organizational Communication: </STRONG> :: 161 :: The School of Communication at The Ohio State University invites applicants for an :: 162 :: <STRONG> assistant professor position in the area of group, network, or organizational communication </STRONG> :: 163 :: , with an emphasis on topics including small group interactions, organizational structures and communication networks, and communication campaigns. The ideal candidate will be able to intersect with the strengths of the School in one or more of the following areas: health, politics, mass communication, or communication technology. :: 164 :: The School is committed to empirical, social-scientific research on communication processes, either basic or applied, making original and substantively important contributions and is regularly ranked among the top communication research programs in the country. We seek colleagues who will help us continue this tradition and can envision research projects and courses that will be attractive to graduate and undergraduate students from within the major, and speak to the interests and needs of non-majors. All of our positions involve teaching, service and a research component, and we have recently renovated a number of research labs and teaching facilities to support quality research and teaching. :: 165 :: To build a diverse workforce Ohio State encourages applications from individuals with disabilities, minorities, veterans, and women. EEO/AA employer. :: 166 :: Job Requirements :: 167 :: Candidates must have a Ph.D. degree in communication or related social science or be ABD and earn the Ph.D. prior to September 2012. Applicants should have a demonstrated record or strong likelihood of publication in top-tier journals in the field of communication as well as evidence of effective collegiate teaching. :: 168 :: Deadline for full consideration for this position is :: 169 :: <STRONG> September 23, 2011 </STRONG> :: 170 :: . Interested candidates should send a cover letter, curriculum vita, at least one published research sample, evidence of successful collegiate teaching, and three letters of reference to: William Eveland, Search Committee Chair, OSU School of Communication, 3016 Derby Hall, 154 North Oval Mall, Columbus, Ohio 43210. Informal queries or applications via email are also welcome at :: 171 :: jobs.comm@osu.edu :: 172 :: mailto:jobs.comm@osu.edu :: 173 :: . :: 174 :: <STRONG> Please explicitly identify the position for which you are applying, as we are conducting four separate searches in 2011-2012. </STRONG> :: 175 :: Additional information about the School and the University is available at :: 176 :: http://www.comm.ohio-state.edu :: 177 :: http://www.comm.ohio-state.edu/ :: 178 :: . :: 179 :: The OSU campus is strategically located in Columbus, the capital city of Ohio. Columbus is the center of a rapidly growing and diverse metropolitan area with a population of over 1.5 million. It is a friendly city with a high quality of life. The area offers a wide range of affordable housing, many cultural and recreational opportunities, and a strong economy based on government as well as service, transportation and technology-based industries. Columbus has consistently been rated as one of the Top U.S. cities for quality of life. :: 153 :: <STRONG> assistant professor </STRONG> :: 154 :: of public relations positions to begin August 2012. :: 155 :: Ideal candidates will have the ability to teach basic and advanced courses in 146 :: 	# :: 147 :: 	Apply For Job :: 148 :: 	# :: 149 :: 	Job Description :: 150 :: 	Nanyang Technological University (NTU) is an internationally renowned tertiary education institution. NTU, together with its predecessor, Nanyang University, has offered university education in Singapore since 1955. NTU boasts a strong engineering college that is ranked among the best globally. Committed to our mission of educating leaders and advancing knowledge for Singapore and beyond, we have built global programs and established strong links with leading institutions around the world. NTU’s 200-hectare campus is among the most advanced in the academic world. The campus now houses 33,000 undergraduate and postgraduate students, and 3,300 teaching and research staff. :: 151 :: <BR/> :: 152 :: <BR/> :: 153 :: <STRONG> 1. CAREER OPPORTUNITIES IN THE SCHOOL OF CHEMICAL AND BIOMEDICAL ENGINEERING </STRONG> :: 154 :: <BR/> :: 155 :: The chemical and biomedical industries in Singapore have seen very healthy growth in recent years. With the increasing demand for chemical engineers and bioengineers, a School of Chemical and Biomedical Engineering has been established in NTU. The School, comprising Division of Chemical and Biomolecular Engineering and Division of Bioengineering, aims to empower a generation of graduates with new perspectives in engineering practices to meet the challenges of the chemical and biomedical industries around the globe. :: 156 :: <BR/> :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <STRONG> Tenure-track Assistant Professor/Associate Professor/Professor Positions </STRONG> :: 159 :: <BR/> :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: The School invites applications for tenure-track faculty appointments at the Assistant, Associate or Full Professor level in: :: 162 :: <BR/> :: 163 :: <BR/> :: 164 :: <STRONG> Chemical and Biomolecular Engineering </STRONG> :: 165 :: <BR/> :: 166 :: Candidates must have at least a B.Sc. or B.Eng. in Chemical Engineering, a Ph.D. in Chemical Engineering or other closely related areas from reputable universities. Research expertise is required in one of the following areas: Process Systems Engineering, Product and Process Design, Pharmaceutical Engineering, Polymers and Soft Materials, and Separations Technology. Creative and energetic individuals who show extraordinary promise or accomplishment in other related areas will also be considered. :: 167 :: <BR/> :: 168 :: <BR/> :: 169 :: <STRONG> Bioengineering </STRONG> :: 170 :: <BR/> :: 171 :: Candidates must have at least a B.Sc. or B.Eng. in Life Sciences, Mechanical Engineering, Electrical Engineering, Computer Science/ Engineering or Bioengineering, a Ph.D. in Bioengineering or other closely related areas from reputable universities. Research expertise is required in one of the following areas: Biomechanics, Bioimaging, Biomedical Devices, Tissue Engineering, Biomaterials, Systems Biology, Computational Biology and Bio-nanotechnology. :: 172 :: <BR/> :: 173 :: <BR/> :: 174 :: In addition to the qualifications and research expertise, candidates should have interests in undergraduate and graduate teaching, a track record of excellent publications and preferably successful grant applications. :: 175 :: <BR/> :: 176 :: <BR/> :: 177 :: <STRONG> Lecturer/Senior Lecturer Positions </STRONG> :: 178 :: <BR/> :: 179 :: <BR/> :: 180 :: The School invites applications for multiple non-tenure track lecturer and senior lecturer positions. Duties will include teaching starting January 2012 in core chemical engineering / bioengineering courses, elective courses or final year design projects relevant to the semiconductor / petroleum / pharmaceutical / healthcare / biomedical industry. :: 181 :: <BR/> :: 182 :: <BR/> :: 183 :: Candidates must have at least a B.Sc. or B.Eng. in Chemical Engineering, Bioengineering or other closely related areas, a Ph.D. or Master degree in relevant disciplines from reputable universities. In addition, candidates must have demonstrated teaching excellence in undergraduate teaching. Relevant industrial experiences are needed for teaching elective courses or final year design projects. :: 184 :: <BR/> :: 185 :: <BR/> :: 186 :: <STRONG> 2. EMOLUMENTS AND GENERAL TERMS & CONDITIONS OF SERVICE </STRONG> :: 187 :: <BR/> :: 188 :: The commencing salary will depend on the candidate's qualifications, experience and the level of appointment offered. The successful candidate will join an established group of physicians and surgeons in one of the top 50 Heart Centers in the United States. VCU Medical Center has one of the largest heart transplant and device programs in Virginia and provides the full spectrum of treatment modalities for advanced heart failure, acute cardiac care and electrophysiology. We are also a leader in providing care for patients with cardiac arrest (e.g. hypothermia) and acute myocardial infarction. We are dedicated to building a preeminent program for academic discovery and are committed to excellent clinical care for heart failure patients. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: Candidate must be a BC/BE cardiologist with demonstrated leadership and clinical skills in at least one of the following areas: advanced heart failure, ischemic heart disease, interventional cardiology, non-invasive imaging and/or basic science. Candidate will work collaboratively with the Division Chief of Cardiothoracic Surgery and his faculty and nursing leadership. Candidate should be clinically oriented and possess sufficient research and teaching experience to be eligible for academic appointment. The candidate must be able to communicate effectively and work with a large multidisciplinary program. The successful candidate will be expected to participate in teaching and educational programs. Academic rank and compensation are dependent upon qualifications. Applicants must be eligible for medical licensure in the State of Virginia. Faculty member will be required to have a well developed scholarly/research portfolio with evidence of multi-disciplinary applications and external funding appropriate to complement and expand existing expertise in the Division of Cardiology. In addition to a focus on communication technologies, candidates may have a particular interest in a context area or population. :: 164 :: The School is committed to empirical, social-scientific research on communication processes, either basic or applied, making original and substantively important contributions and is regularly ranked among the top communication research programs in the country. Applicants should have a demonstrated record or strong likelihood of publication in top-tier journals in the field of communication as well as evidence of effective collegiate teaching. :: 168 :: Deadline for full consideration for this position is :: 169 :: <STRONG> September 23, 2011 </STRONG> :: 170 :: . The qualified individual should be Board Eligible/Board Certified in Endocrinology and Metabolism, The candidate must qualify for an appointment at the Assistant or Associate Professor level, and have demonstrated expertise in diabetes and metabolism, thyroid disorders or metabolic bone disease. She/he must demonstrate experience working in and fostering a diverse faculty, staff and student environment or a commitment to do so as a faculty member at Virginia Commonwealth University. The successful candidate will participate as Clinician-Educator in the teaching and mentoring of medical students, residents and endocrinology fellows in inpatient and outpatient settings, will establish outpatient clinics in general endocrinology, diabetes and other areas of interest and will contribute to the overall scholarly and research activities of the Division. :: 155 :: Virginia Commonwealth University is an urban university with over 32,000 students located in Richmond, Virginia, two hours south of Washington D.C. As one of the nation's top research universities it attracts more than $255 million a year in sponsored research funding. Twenty-seven VCU graduate and professional programs rank among the best in the nation in :: 156 :: <EM> US News & World Report's </EM> :: 157 :: America's Best Graduate Schools. :: 158 :: VCU Medical Center is one of the nation's leading academic medical centers. It includes the 780 bed MCV Hospitals and outpatient clinics, MCV Physicians - a 600 physician-faculty group practice and the health sciences schools of VCU. It offers state-of-the-art care in more than 200 specialty areas and is the region's only Level 1 Trauma Center. :: 159 :: Richmond, the state capital, is situated between the Shenandoah Mountains and the Virginia/North Carolina coast. This central location provides an affordable lifestyle with easy access to beaches, mountains and other metropolitan areas on the east coast. :: 160 :: Interested candidates should contact :: 161 :: <STRONG> Robert W. :: 153 :: <BR/> :: 154 :: <BR/> :: 155 :: Candidates with an MFA and/or Ph.D., advanced experience in film and digital production and a strong commitment to liberal arts teaching are invited to apply. :: 156 :: <BR/> :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: The ideal candidate will combine experience in independent narrative cinema with an active production and exhibition record. :: 159 :: Fax: :: 160 :: 614-292-4299 :: 161 :: 	Save Job :: 162 :: 	# :: 163 :: 	E-mail Job :: 164 :: 	# :: 165 :: 	Print Job :: 166 :: 	# :: 167 :: 	 	 	Job Description :: 168 :: 	The Ohio State University College of Social Work invites applications for two tenure-track faculty positions, rank open, beginning September 2012. Social work is the fastest growing major at this research intensive university and we are growing our faculty to keep pace with the demand for exceptional scholars and educators. Successful candidates will be capable educators for our three degree programs: BSSW, MSW, and PhD. We are interested in recruiting the best candidates for our forward-moving scientific agenda: candidates who have demonstrated strong research and scholarship capacity. We are also recruiting strong educators who fit our redesigned curricula which will begin implementation in autumn 2012. The College of Social Work encourages education and scholarship related to implementing our vision “ :: 169 :: <EM> Embrace Difference. Seek Justice. Be the Change. </EM> :: 170 :: ” and translational or intervention research collaborations. Candidates must have or be scheduled to complete an earned doctorate in social work or related field; one or more social work degrees preferred. Applicants expecting to teach practice methods must have an MSW degree and at least two years post-MSW practice experience. :: 171 :: The College of Social Work at the Ohio State University is the longest continuously accredited public social work program in the United States. The Ohio State University, an extensive doctoral/research institution, is located in Ohio’s vibrant state capital, Columbus, within a diverse metropolitan region—the largest in the state and 15 :: 172 :: <SUP> th </SUP> :: 173 :: largest in the nation. Successful candidates will join our 30 faculty and six field staff and engage with our student body of about 200 BSSW, 450 MSW, and 40 doctoral level students. For more information, visit our website at csw.osu.edu. :: 174 :: Review of applications will begin immediately and continue until positions are filled. Initial screening interviews are expected to take place during late October, with campus visit invitations beginning November-December, 2011. Please submit an electronic application package (subject line: FACAPP) that includes separate Word® or pdf attachments with: (1) a concise letter of application that addresses how your professional goals align with curriculum and research goals for the College, (2) a curriculum vitae, (3) a single-authored writing sample, (4) summarized teaching evaluations (if available), and (5) three letters of reference. All materials and questions should be directed to: :: 175 :: Dr. Audrey L. 145 :: 	Save Job :: 146 :: 	# :: 147 :: 	E-mail Job :: 148 :: 	# :: 149 :: 	Print Job :: 150 :: 	# :: 151 :: 	Apply For Job :: 152 :: 	# :: 153 :: 	Job Description :: 154 :: 	<STRONG> Job Description </STRONG> :: 155 :: <BR/> :: 156 :: The Prosthodontics Faculty in the School of Dental Medicine is responsible for teaching Prosthodontics to pre-doctoral students in the Section of Prosthodontics of the dental school. This unit is within the Division of General Dentistry. The Prosthodontics Faculty reports directly to the Section Chief of Prosthodontics. The Prosthodontics section works in close cooperation with the Offices of Academic Support, Clinical Affairs, and Dental Education and Informatics to support the School's programs and initiatives. In addition, the section works closely with other Schools and Colleges of East Carolina University and other components of the University of North Carolina, as well as local/regional educational and clinical programs. The Prosthodontics Faculty supports the development and implementation of the Prosthodontic aspects of the preclinical and clinical curriculum taught to the dental students. Specific duties include: Working closely with the Section Chief of Prosthodontics and the Assistant Dean for Dental Education and Informatics in curriculum development and implementation related to Prosthodontics for the general dentist. Working closely with the Section Chief of Prosthodontics and the Associate Dean for Clinical Affairs in the development and implementation of the preclinical, clinical, and academic components of the electronic dental record related to Prosthodontics. Working closely with the Assistant Dean for Dental Education and Informatics and other informatics personnel to optimize the use of technology to support the section's teaching programs. Helping ensure that the dental students are competent in the management of patients requiring prosthodontics. Coordinate and help deliver curricular content related to prosthodontics in the simulation lab and didactic settings. Willingness and ability to cover pre-doctoral students in the clinical setting in procedures outside of the field of Prosthodontics as pertaining to the General Dentistry Model of the School of Dental Medicine. Conducting basic and/or clinical research, and other scholarly activities that will help qualify for appropriate promotion. Preparing accreditation and other program documentation as needed. Actively participating in the school's faculty practice plan. Seeking to serve on committees and boards for state/federal government agencies, professional societies, and within the school. Assisting the Chair of General Dentistry and the Associate Dean for Clinical Affairs in quality assurance and improvement, and compliance efforts. Responding to assignments from the Chair of General Dentistry and the Dean of the School of Dental Medicine essential to section's and school's operations. Attending meetings and representing the School in internal and external venues as requested by the Chair of General Dentistry or the Dean. Representing the School to external constituencies as appropriate. Performing other duties and assuming additional responsibilities as assigned by the Chair of General Dentistry or the Dean. Fixed-term or tenure-track position available. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: <STRONG> Minimum Qualifications </STRONG> :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: Required Qualifications DMD, DDS or equivalent dental degree from an appropriately accredited institution. Commitment to building teams in planning and to identify and resolve problems. Commitment to conducting basic and/or clinical research, and other scholarly activities that will help qualify for appropriate promotion. Preferred Qualifications Training in a Prosthodontics Residency, Advanced Education in General Dentistry residency, or General Practice Residency. Substantial clinical experience with implant supported prosthodontics. Commitment to evidence-based teaching and practice. Experience in preparing and teaching preclinical and clinical aspects of prosthodontics. Willingness to apply academic experiences of contemporary dental education and traditional educational values to the Service Learning model. :: 162 :: <BR/> :: 163 :: <BR/> :: 164 :: <STRONG> Special Instructions to Applicants </STRONG> :: 165 :: <BR/> :: 166 :: East Carolina University requires applicants to submit a candidate profile online in order to be considered for the position. :: Kenneth A. Ellenbogen, M.D. :: 142 :: Email Address: :: 143 :: kellenbogen@mcvh-vcu.edu :: 144 :: mailto:kellenbogen@mcvh-vcu.edu :: 145 :: 	Save Job :: 146 :: 	# :: 147 :: 	E-mail Job :: 148 :: 	# :: 149 :: 	Print Job :: 150 :: 	# :: 151 :: 	 	 	Job Description :: 152 :: 	Director of Coronary Intensive Care Unit :: 153 :: <STRONG> Division of Cardiology </STRONG> :: 154 :: <STRONG> MCV Physicians </STRONG> :: 155 :: <STRONG> Richmond, Virginia </STRONG> :: 156 :: Virginia Commonwealth University Medical Center is seeking a Medical Director to lead its 14-bed coronary intensive care unit. The successful candidate will join an established group of physicians and surgeons in one of the top 50 Heart Centers in the United States. VCU Medical Center has one of the largest heart transplant and device programs in Virginia and provides the full spectrum of treatment modalities for advanced heart failure, acute cardiac care and electrophysiology. We are also a leader in providing care for patients with cardiac arrest (e.g. hypothermia) and acute myocardial infarction. We are dedicated to building a preeminent program for academic discovery and are committed to excellent clinical care for heart failure patients. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: Candidate must be a BC/BE cardiologist with demonstrated leadership and clinical skills in at least one of the following areas: advanced heart failure, ischemic heart disease, interventional cardiology, non-invasive imaging and/or basic science. The physician will be expected to provide medical leadership to this unit that will enhance and foster national prominence through clinical, education and research activities. Candidate will work collaboratively with the Division Chief of Cardiothoracic Surgery and his faculty and nursing leadership. Candidate should be clinically oriented and possess sufficient research and teaching experience to be eligible for academic appointment. The candidate must be able to communicate effectively and work with a large multidisciplinary program. The successful candidate will be expected to participate in teaching and educational programs. Academic rank and compensation are dependent upon qualifications. Applicants must be eligible for medical licensure in the State of Virginia. Faculty member will be required to have a well developed scholarly/research portfolio with evidence of multi-disciplinary applications and external funding appropriate to complement and expand existing expertise in the Division of Cardiology. Demonstrated experience working in and fostering a diverse faculty, staff, and student environment or commitment to do so as a faculty member at VCU. :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: <BR/> :: 162 :: Qualified applicants are invited to submit a cover letter, current CV with bibliography, and list of references with full contact information to: :: 163 :: <STRONG> Kenneth A. http://ecu.peopleadmin.com/applicants/Central?quickFind=65483&jtsrc=www.insightintodiversity.com&jtrfr=www.peopleadmin.com&adorig=PA :: 145 :: 	Save Job :: 146 :: 	# :: 147 :: 	E-mail Job :: 148 :: 	# :: 149 :: 	Print Job :: 150 :: 	# :: 151 :: 	Apply For Job :: 152 :: 	# :: 153 :: 	Job Description :: 154 :: 	<STRONG> Job Description </STRONG> :: 155 :: <BR/> :: 156 :: The Director of Diversity and Cultural Competence Management reports through the Senior Director to the Associate Provost for Equity, Diversity and Community Relations. Functions of this position include: Identifies and engages emerging populations throughout the multi-constituency base of the Equity, Diversity and Community Relations unit through programming, outreach and special initiatives. Research and implement best practice for engaging emerging populations in this region. Collaborates and supports the Associate Provost with the engage pre-collegiate students and communities to prepare a pipeline of diverse academic talent from emerging populations. Identifies evolving trends in diversity and technology to better inform innovative learning strategies for cultural competence development programs for students, faculty and staff. Directs the integration of advanced learning technology into all educational, experiential and outreach opportunities offered by the Equity, Diversity and Community Relations unit. Incorporates cutting edge technology across the unit and works collaboratively with the Senior Director and EDC Coordinator to advance a contemporary communication infrastructure for the unit. Engages internal and external collaborative partners to advance the unit's work. Develops technology based co-curricular programs and activities designed to develop a more culturally competent and globally aware campus community. Provides data and consulting support to the equity, diversity and affirmative action efforts of the unit. Provides data and information technology consultation to inform the design of cultural competence/pre-professional educational programs by the Diversity Expert In Residence and Associate Provost. Provides strategic planning support to the Associate Provost, Senior Director and unit and develops all Equity, Diversity and Community Relations' diversity related reports and publications. Liaises with IPAR and serves as the EDC point of contact for each division, college and library in the management and review of diversity action plans, goals and objectives. Compile, review and organize data to inform and support the goals for EDC and the annual thematic areas of emphasis for the Chancellor's Diversity Leadership Cabinet and Diversity Liaison Group. Creates educational outreach materials for the unit to inform the university, community and specific audiences regarding diversity and equity progress. Conducts small scale studies as commissioned by the Associate Provost on topics germane to the access and opportunities of students, faculty and staff of color, women, and persons with disability, socio-economically challenged employees, veterans, gay, lesbian or bisexual persons and persons of all religious affiliations. Monitors diversity and equity related intelligent indicators and progress consistent with the institution's diversity framework. Creates office tracking and monitoring systems for EDC educational programs, outreach and pipeline efforts. Oversees a comprehensive reporting system to effectively monitor, analyze and benchmark progress in diversity and equity. Seeks external funding for the unit's internal, external and community related projects through grant research and writing. The Director collaborates with the Associate Provost to coordinate special programs to engage experts in the diversity, inclusion and cultural competence fields. Provides other diversity and equity services as deemed appropriate to the functioning of the Equity, Diversity and Community Relations unit. Opportunities for participation on divisional, university and national committees exist as assigned by the Associate Provost for Equity, Diversity and Community Relations. :: 157 :: <BR/> :: 158 :: <BR/> :: 159 :: <STRONG> Minimum Qualifications </STRONG> :: 160 :: <BR/> :: 161 :: Masters Degree in education, business, social work, technology, psychology or a related field from an appropriately accredited institution. Experience in diversity, and /or equity programs, statistics and research methodology. Experience in human relations, equity, diversity, student affairs, globalism, cultural studies or related area. Demonstrated ability to work effectively with a culturally diverse workforce and provide leadership in organizational change. Preferred Qualifications: Minimum of two years experience with responsibility in the management of diversity related programs. Clear understanding of diversity, equity and cultural competence practice in higher education. :: 162 :: <BR/> :: 163 :: <BR/> :: 164 :: <STRONG> Special Instructions to Applicants </STRONG> :: 165 :: <BR/> :: 166 :: Candidates should submit online a letter of application, resume, and a list of three references including contact information. :: 167 :: APPLY FOR THIS JOB :: 168 :: Apply URL: :: 169 :: http://ecu.peopleadmin.com/applicants/Central?quic... :: 170 :: http://ecu.peopleadmin.com/applicants/Central?quickFind=65483&jtsrc=www.insightintodiversity.com&jtrfr=www.peopleadmin.com&adorig=PA :: 171 :: Save Job :: 172 :: # :: 173 :: E-mail Job :: 174 :: # :: 175 :: Print Job :: 176 :: # :: 177 :: Apply For Job :: 178 :: # :: 179 :: 	Back to Results :: 180 :: 	/c/search_results.cfm?vnet=0&t735=&max=100&t730=&t731=&site%5Fid=9533&jb=8519737 :: 181 :: 	<BR/> :: 182 :: 	<B> Questions/Feedback </B> :: 183 :: 	<BR/> :: 184 :: 	If you need assistance or have feedback about this service :: 185 :: 	contact customer service :: 186 :: 	mailto:custserv@jobtarget.com :: 187 :: 	. :: 188 :: 	http://careers.insightintodiversity.com:80/images/spacerclear.gif :: 189 :: 	<BR/> :: 190 :: 	INSIGHT Into Diversity is the largest and oldest diversity employment magazine and website in higher education today. :: 191 :: 	<BR/> :: 192 :: 	Launched 35 years ago as a resource to assist institutions in complying with equal opportunity employment laws, :: 193 :: 	<BR/> :: 194 :: 	INSIGHT Into Diversity is now a premier source of information for half a million readers each month seeking in-depth news, :: 195 :: 	<BR/> :: 196 :: 	reports and commentary on issues surrounding all aspects of diversity and inclusion. :: 	E-mail Job :: 156 :: 	# :: 157 :: 	Print Job :: 158 :: 	# :: 159 :: 	 	 	Job Description :: 160 :: 	<STRONG> Group, Network, or Organizational Communication: </STRONG> :: 161 :: The School of Communication at The Ohio State University invites applicants for an :: 162 :: <STRONG> assistant professor position in the area of group, network, or organizational communication </STRONG> :: 163 :: , with an emphasis on topics including small group interactions, organizational structures and communication networks, and communication campaigns. The ideal candidate will be able to intersect with the strengths of the School in one or more of the following areas: health, politics, mass communication, or communication technology. :: 164 :: The School is committed to empirical, social-scientific research on communication processes, either basic or applied, making original and substantively important contributions and is regularly ranked among the top communication research programs in the country. We seek colleagues who will help us continue this tradition and can envision research projects and courses that will be attractive to graduate and undergraduate students from within the major, and speak to the interests and needs of non-majors. All of our positions involve teaching, service and a research component, and we have recently renovated a number of research labs and teaching facilities to support quality research and teaching. :: 165 :: To build a diverse workforce Ohio State encourages applications from individuals with disabilities, minorities, veterans, and women. EEO/AA employer. :: 166 :: Job Requirements :: 167 :: Candidates must have a Ph.D. degree in communication or related social science or be ABD and earn the Ph.D. prior to September 2012. Applicants should have a demonstrated record or strong likelihood of publication in top-tier journals in the field of communication as well as evidence of effective collegiate teaching. :: 168 :: Deadline for full consideration for this position is :: 169 :: <STRONG> September 23, 2011 </STRONG> :: 170 :: . Interested candidates should send a cover letter, curriculum vita, at least one published research sample, evidence of successful collegiate teaching, and three letters of reference to: William Eveland, Search Committee Chair, OSU School of Communication, 3016 Derby Hall, 154 North Oval Mall, Columbus, Ohio 43210. Informal queries or applications via email are also welcome at :: 171 :: jobs.comm@osu.edu :: 172 :: mailto:jobs.comm@osu.edu :: 173 :: . :: 174 :: <STRONG> Please explicitly identify the position for which you are applying, as we are conducting four separate searches in 2011-2012. </STRONG> :: 175 :: Additional information about the School and the University is available at :: 176 :: http://www.comm.ohio-state.edu :: 177 :: http://www.comm.ohio-state.edu/ :: 178 :: . :: 179 :: The OSU campus is strategically located in Columbus, the capital city of Ohio. Columbus is the center of a rapidly growing and diverse metropolitan area with a population of over 1.5 million. It is a friendly city with a high quality of life. The area offers a wide range of affordable housing, many cultural and recreational opportunities, and a strong economy based on government as well as service, transportation and technology-based industries. Columbus has consistently been rated as one of the Top U.S. cities for quality of life.
